<div id="review_192328004" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192328004" />
    <a title="Nick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2973164-nick"><img alt="Nick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312829623p2/2973164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192328004?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick" href="/user/show/2973164-nick">Nick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385260121" href="/book/show/862121.Grass">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2973164-nick?shelf=sci-fizzle">sci-fizzle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192328004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13131768400959278411">Man, this was a weird one. It was a bit of a ponderous read for me. There was good and bad in <i>Grass</i>, and I think other people might enjoy it more than I did.<br/><br/>I said in my last status update for this book that reading it was "like having a vivid, strange nightmare that didn't quite make sense." I think this captures both the good and the bad of <i>Grass</i>. Sheri Tepper's world building is <i>excellent</i>. Her universe is nuanced, vibrant, original and memorable. Unfortunately, that's really where my praise e</span>
  <span id="freeText13131768400959278411" style="display:none">Man, this was a weird one. It was a bit of a ponderous read for me. There was good and bad in <i>Grass</i>, and I think other people might enjoy it more than I did.<br /><br />I said in my last status update for this book that reading it was "like having a vivid, strange nightmare that didn't quite make sense." I think this captures both the good and the bad of <i>Grass</i>. Sheri Tepper's world building is <i>excellent</i>. Her universe is nuanced, vibrant, original and memorable. Unfortunately, that's really where my praise ends.<br /><br />The characters feel like stock characters generated by a machine. They lack a certain multi-faceted aspect that better characters would possess. Her dialogue doesn't seem realistic. When I say "realistic" I'm not referring to something like the aristocratically-toned speech of some of the characters, I'm referring to the actual content of their conversations. They just don't have conversations like real people would. It seems like they're having their conversations simply for the benefit of the story and the reader. The characters always do exactly what you expect they will do. I felt Brother Mainoa was written a little better than the rest of them. <br /><br />I think the characters suffer from a lot of the same problems you typically find in a lot of hard sci-fi novels, particularly authors like Isaac Asimov. However, I think the problem becomes more glaring in <i>Grass</i> because it's more of a <i>fantastic adventure story with surprising catches</i> and less of a <i>wouldn't it be interesting if RANDOM SCI-FI EVENT happened</i> story. (One could argue that <i>Grass</i> is both of these kinds of stories, but I feel that is principally the former.) If I'm reading a fantastic adventure story, I damn well better care about the characters more than say, <i>Nightfall</i>, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[where I just want to see what the hell happens to all the aliens when the suns blink out and they go CRAZY <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. (the spoiler is from <i>Nightfall</i>.)<br /><br />The pace of the book is problematic at best. It seems to unnecessarily meander at times, leaving the reader yawning and wondering why the plot isn't being advanced. This comes from a guy whose favorite book is <i>Moby Dick</i>.<br /><br />I feel that what I've written above should be true for anyone who reads <i>Grass</i>, but the following are more things I just may have personally disliked.<br /><br />I didn't give a good goddamn about any of the spiritual conflicts in the book. Maybe it was because the characters weren't very good, but every time Marjorie started to whine about her spiritual conflict I wanted to gouge out my eyes with an escargot fork, which would have been appropriate given the highfalutin propensities of a great deal of <i>Grass'</i> characters. <br /><br />I was kind of turned off by the "horse worship" in the book. There's tons of horsemanship porn in this book. By horsemanship porn, I mean lots of descriptions about the quirks of particular horses, the great detail put into their names (El Dia Octavo, Her Majesty (*BARF*), etc.), the emotional connection of human and horse, and all that jazz. I enjoyed riding quite a bit when I was youth, and I get being into horsemanship and horses themselves. However, there's so much "horsemanship porn" in the book that it becomes distracting and irritating. <br /><br />If you're a tough guy who walks around in his house in Space Marine armor barbecuing meat and eating it <i>right off the bone</i> you'll probably be turned off by the (at times) melodramatic writing style. Of course, if that bothers you the odds are the horsemanship porn will bother you too. I love the hell out of flowers and butterflies and it got to me.<br /><br />Really, you should check out some flowers and butterflies. They're much cheaper to enjoy than those Warhammer 40,000 models you've been buying and painting. If it makes you feel better about it, glue a plastic tank cannon or a giant chainsaw on a butterfly. The best of both worlds!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13131768400959278411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291915-lauren?shelf=scifi-speculative">scifi-speculative</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2781808057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3107613747735475896">First half - Intriguing world building, curious where this will go with its creatures and societal structure.<br/><br/>Second half - This book lost me and I don't even care to be found. Devolved into such a mess. Not sure why this is so highly rated.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4388309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13919627798836327749">A family of ambassadors comes to the planet Grass, inhabited by isolated, rural aristrocrat families and one large commoner town, to figure out why it's the only human-inhabited planet where people are dying of plague. Really great human-alien interaction as well as between humans of extremely different cultures. The whole thing takes place in a universe dominated by a religion called Sanctity that is trying to cover up the existence of the plague. On the planet, the aristocrats could care less </span>
  <span id="freeText13919627798836327749" style="display:none">A family of ambassadors comes to the planet Grass, inhabited by isolated, rural aristrocrat families and one large commoner town, to figure out why it's the only human-inhabited planet where people are dying of plague. Really great human-alien interaction as well as between humans of extremely different cultures. The whole thing takes place in a universe dominated by a religion called Sanctity that is trying to cover up the existence of the plague. On the planet, the aristocrats could care less whether every other human on all other worlds dies of plague. Meanwhile, the aristocrats' relations with the alien species on the planet seem just a little too strange. The ambassador family must contend with all of this as they try to figure out the answers while not letting their family unit completely implode. I really enjoyed this book (and enjoyed it WAY more than the other Tepper book i've read, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104344.The_Gate_to_Women_s_Country" title="The Gate to Women's Country by Sheri S. Tepper" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gate to Women's Country</a>.<br /><br />The other good thing is that, at some point during the book, you get at least a glimpse, if not way more, into pretty much *every* culture encountered: aristocrats, commoners, Sanctity, plague-ridden communities, alien species, repentant monks also living on the planet, etc. It gets a little dizzying as there are so many societies introduced, but it all fits together really nicely, and avoids the problem I often have with this kind of book, which is "But what about the ____ people? What do they think?"</span>
  <a data-text-id="13919627798836327749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1672621653926468738">The beginning was probably the best: the setup, the mysteries, the danger, and Grass. So much grass. Grass the planet is amazing.<br/><br/>Marjorie slowly became a layered character that I wanted to read about, but by the end, this was noticeably conveniently plotted (ooo, a letter fell out of his pocket! the nasty hierarch just runs away! wait, is this about a plague or religion or aliens or exobiology or a failed marriage or...) and it was heavy handed on the religious themes.<br/><br/>I've really enjoyed religio</span>
  <span id="freeText1672621653926468738" style="display:none">The beginning was probably the best: the setup, the mysteries, the danger, and Grass. So much grass. Grass the planet is amazing.<br /><br />Marjorie slowly became a layered character that I wanted to read about, but by the end, this was noticeably conveniently plotted (ooo, a letter fell out of his pocket! the nasty hierarch just runs away! wait, is this about a plague or religion or aliens or exobiology or a failed marriage or...) and it was heavy handed on the religious themes.<br /><br />I've really enjoyed religion in other SFF novels, but honestly, this was nowhere near as subtle or masterful or thought-provoking as Hyperion Cantos. There was also a surprising amount of hateful sexism thrown in, tightly linked with religion. That tired me out to read. I didn't fully understand what the *point* of all that was. Especially those Green Brothers <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[who are bad news anyway - they're almost comically villainous - but you also randomly have to have a select few go on a useless evil assassin quest and threaten rape on our heroine? isn't it bad enough already they were sent to willingly and gleefully MURDER people? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The best part at the end? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Marjorie finally tells her asshole masculinity-obsessed cheater of a husband and their enabling confessor priest to both go to hell because she FINALLY sees how blatantly they still want to control her as a woman and wife. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_516533866" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/516533866" />
    <a title="Mike Franklin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16460451-mike-franklin"><img alt="Mike Franklin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358524699p2/16460451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/516533866?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike Franklin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike Franklin" href="/user/show/16460451-mike-franklin">Mike Franklin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16460451-mike-franklin?shelf=sf-masterworks">sf-masterworks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16460451-mike-franklin?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer516533866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13768132438499514340">I have given Grass 4 stars though I would have given it 4.5 if I could but it just didn't quite make it to my top rating.<br/><br/>It is, however, a very good book; thought provoking, entertaining and believable (mostly).<br/><br/>The first half of the book has an almost claustrophobic feel to it that put me in mind of a Hitchcock movie. The full picture is deliberately hidden from us (somewhat crudely at the beginning of the book), instead the writing is filled with a sense of building threat from a menance that s</span>
  <span id="freeText13768132438499514340" style="display:none">I have given Grass 4 stars though I would have given it 4.5 if I could but it just didn't quite make it to my top rating.<br /><br />It is, however, a very good book; thought provoking, entertaining and believable (mostly).<br /><br />The first half of the book has an almost claustrophobic feel to it that put me in mind of a Hitchcock movie. The full picture is deliberately hidden from us (somewhat crudely at the beginning of the book), instead the writing is filled with a sense of building threat from a menance that stays just beyond our knowledge.<br /><br />The main revelation point comes around half way through the book and I worried whether it had peaked too early. However, though the sense of claustrophobia diminishes, the sense of imminent threat and danger persists and the story pace starts picking up; never really relenting until the final conclusion, which sadly I thought was a little too neat and the use of a letter to wrap up the loose ends seemed a little cheap. One of the reasons it didn't get the 5 star rating from me.<br /><br />I find it interesting that Tepper, well known as a feminist writer, has chosen to set her book in a society controlled by religion, both 'Sanctity' and 'Old Catholic' and both of those religions portrayed as pretty fundamentalist in nature and very definitely male dominated. What I found strange is that, despite being written in 1989 by a feminist and being set far in the future, the position of women in society seems to me more akin to the earliest part of the 20th century - maybe the 30s or 40s - and the religious influence even earlier than that; almost medieval. Whilst I didn't have a problem with this it didn't quite sit right with me and I did find the outdated dogma - aristocracy with their own private priests, regular confession to keep your soul clean, etc. - a little annoying and not really necessary. It would have been perfectly reasonable to have had the Green Brothers and explored the idea of original sin without needing to make religion as dominant as it was.<br /><br />All that said, Tepper has come up with fascinating aliens and a plot that moves smoothly from the Hitchcock-like, suspenseful first half to the action packed, fast paced second half, making a great read that leaves you with stuff to think about. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13768132438499514340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_413783468" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/413783468" />
    <a title="Neil Powell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3826800-neil-powell"><img alt="Neil Powell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1276174796p2/3826800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/413783468?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil Powell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil Powell" href="/user/show/3826800-neil-powell">Neil Powell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer413783468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12696236456689399407">An odd read. Like alot of sci-fi, this book is packed full of ideas. Some of these are very thought provoking and insightful, others less so.<br/><br/>I thought the story started strongly, a nice sense of brooding and mystery is generated when the main protagonists arrive on the planet Grass. However, the first of several "reveals" come a little too early, and comes at the expense of a interesting subplot concerning a breakaway religious sect. <br/><br/>The several other twists aren't particularly convincing, logic</span>
  <span id="freeText12696236456689399407" style="display:none">An odd read. Like alot of sci-fi, this book is packed full of ideas. Some of these are very thought provoking and insightful, others less so.<br /><br />I thought the story started strongly, a nice sense of brooding and mystery is generated when the main protagonists arrive on the planet Grass. However, the first of several "reveals" come a little too early, and comes at the expense of a interesting subplot concerning a breakaway religious sect. <br /><br />The several other twists aren't particularly convincing, logical or explained in any real way, and the finale does seem a little rushed.<br /><br />There are things to enjoy: some of the characters are very well constructed and have real depth. In particular the lead female (Marjorie). The writing is at times beautifully descriptive, haunting and often quite disturbing. Personally I found it a little horse heavy in places (equine fans should love it!).<br /><br />I understand it is part of a trilogy, and I'm sufficiently interested to potentially give the other books a go </span>
  <a data-text-id="12696236456689399407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_50625073" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50625073" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1250280-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1238195081p2/1250280.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50625073?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/1250280-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250280-richard?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250280-richard?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250280-richard?shelf=sf-f-bookclub-challenge">sf-f-bookclub-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50625073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13562201871496200316">A wonderful book, with beautifully realised characters and a totally involving setting. It put me in mind of the SF classic 'Dune', but reduced to a more personal, less epic scale with a cogent human future and accessible characters. The planet of Grass and its societies are finely crafted and its alien inhabitants are some of the most intriguing I've come across. The storyline is interesting from the very beginning and continually develops and accelerates. I very rarely give a book a 5 stars (i</span>
  <span id="freeText13562201871496200316" style="display:none">A wonderful book, with beautifully realised characters and a totally involving setting. It put me in mind of the SF classic 'Dune', but reduced to a more personal, less epic scale with a cogent human future and accessible characters. The planet of Grass and its societies are finely crafted and its alien inhabitants are some of the most intriguing I've come across. The storyline is interesting from the very beginning and continually develops and accelerates. I very rarely give a book a 5 stars (it was amazing) rating, but this was the best book I have read for a good many years. I would heartily recommend it to anyone, especially those who enjoyed the essence of 'Dune'.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13562201871496200316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7800646925581441986">This was a reread for me, after a four year gap, and while it definitely felt more problematic this time around, I still enjoyed it very much. I really like Tepper's writing, and despite the last part being utter bobbins, I had just as good a time reading this as I did the first time.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hgGN8lZCQ4BZTdhC3zgzURV9H2Uu779F3FpT2rW8sioeCfjvRdnd7xNUemCKGDSrcVAkRie4N54teT3g3PAP5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DqQFBz/JL5I6DnzT44GRgNHcSADbdgrwzayA461JSCmWrHAaLFKx/XAX3vG2oZZ6tfFzI9Ihgis8j+7ZxAX15Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/20560.Sheri_S_Tepper">About Sheri S. Tepper</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/20560.Sheri_S_Tepper"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1333062700p3/20560.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/20560.Sheri_S_Tepper">Sheri S. Tepper
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
911
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4932419661029680308">Sheri Stewart Tepper was a prolific American author of science fiction, horror and mystery novels; she was particularly known as a feminist science fiction writer, often with an ecofeminist slant.<br/><br/>Born near Littleton, Colorado, for most of her career (1962-1986) she worked for Rocky Mountain Planned Parenthood, where she eventually became Executive Director. She has two children and is married to G</span>
  <span id="freeText4932419661029680308" style="display:none">Sheri Stewart Tepper was a prolific American author of science fiction, horror and mystery novels; she was particularly known as a feminist science fiction writer, often with an ecofeminist slant.<br /><br />Born near Littleton, Colorado, for most of her career (1962-1986) she worked for Rocky Mountain Planned Parenthood, where she eventually became Executive Director. She has two children and is married to Gene Tepper. She operated a guest ranch in Santa Fe, New Mexico.<br /><br />She wrote under several pseudonyms, including <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/317263.A_J__Orde" title="A.J. Orde" rel="nofollow noopener">A.J. Orde</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1092029.E_E__Horlak" title="E.E. Horlak" rel="nofollow noopener">E.E. Horlak</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/870025.B_J__Oliphant" title="B.J. Oliphant" rel="nofollow noopener">B.J. Oliphant</a>. Her early work was published under the name Sheri S. Eberhart.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4932419661029680308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/14066792-grass">Quotes from Grass</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;—Me dijeron que las verdades eternas…<br /><br />—¿Cómo cuáles —Dios se rió—. ¡Si hubiera alguna verdad eterna Yo lo sabría ¡He creado todo un cosmos basado en el cambio y un ser minúsculo viene aquí para hablarme de verdades eternas <br /><br />—No quería ofenderte. Es sólo que… Bueno sí no hay verdades eternas ¿cómo podemos saber dónde está la verdad <br /><br />—No me has ofendido. Nunca creo cosas capaces de ofenderme. En cuanto a la verdad la verdad es lo que está escrito. Todas las cosas de la creación llevan mis intenciones escritas en sí mismas. Las rocas las estrellas los seres minúsculos… Para cada cosa sólo hay un camino natural el camino que Yo he concebido para ella. El problema es que los seres minúsculos escriben libros que contradicen a las rocas y luego dicen que Yo escribí los libros y que las rocas son mentiras. —Se rió. El universo tembló—. Inventan reglas de conducta que ni los ángeles pueden obedecer y dicen que Yo las he ideado. El orgullo de la autoría… —Dejó escapar una risita—. Dicen: «Oh estas palabras son eternas así que deben de haber sido escritas por Dios».&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/402508-me-dijeron-que-las-verdades-eternas-c-mo-cu-les-dios-se">5 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
